After having completed this book for you, which is the last scientific work on medicine in Arabic along with its complement, and being led to a conclusion of it as I proceeded through their explanations and declarations - all that has been done so far concerning your complete satisfaction regarding this Treatise specifically pertaining to surgery.
Since surgery with hands has prevaclty established itself in our region and at the time of my writing (it is possible that this science may even perish): until perhaps such an investigation into it will be lost: nothing remains from these except descriptions found among ancient books, which had their pages torn away by hand; errors occurred to them as a result, resulting ultimately in incomplete intentions on his part and elongated replies. I see myself obliged to perform this treatise according to the manner of its presentation, including forms of cautery knives and remaining instruments for surgical operations: also taking into account additions made by him out of declarations therein which is necessary.
Because a good surgeon cannot be found in our time using his own hands: for the art of medicine is long and requires an author to exercise himself beforehand in the science of anatomy which was narrated by Galen; until he fully knows how members are formed, their connections, separations, bones' structure, muscles’ form, fowl limbs if any (since some birds possess them), scales' number and arrangement on these parts along with other details concerning the exit of blood from vessels thereof.
And because it was said by Hippocrates that the name of this treatise is much but its work only little: and especially so with regard to surgery which pertains chiefly to hands' skill.
We have already told about that thing at the beginning of this book.
For those who are not skilled in anatomy that we have told about it is no longer sufficient; since as they destroy human beinings from errors which happen when these people act without knowledge and science: I myself saw many of such people coming, bearing themselves with their ignorance on this subject, lacking any scientific education or experimental practice.
Which is so that I saw a foolish physician follow up with scrofulous swellings on the neck of a woman and incise some arteries in her throat: blood flowed from this woman until she died between his hands. Now this treatise is divided into three chapters..
Chapter one.
Chapter one is about cautery with fire and hot metal as well as sharp tools; it details the instruments used by caulkers from head to foot and leg, their forms, and related equipment required for surgical operations..
Chapter two., et instrumenta Cauterii: quorum in operation
Chapter two is about incisions and punctures; draining blood vessels (phlebotomy) as well as bleeding through other means such as cauterization or cutting of the skin with a scalpel (ventosis). It also includes techniques for treating wounds, abscesses, fractures, arrows, and similar issues. This chapter is arranged in order according to forms used by caulkers..
Chapter three., et instrumenta Cauterii: quorum sunt ex
Chapter three is about restorations and relocations; treatments for twisted (torsioned) wounds as well as similar issues. This chapter covers techniques from head to foot along with the forms used by caulkers..

Chapter XXXIII.
On extracting the tooth with gold wire:
Whenever there is concussion and motion of the anterior teeth due to percussion or other causes that it cannot be firmly grasped with what you use for chewing (bite-worn restoration) so as not to fall: then apply medicaments suitable for stopping bleeding, but no treatment should take place at this time. The skill in such matters is using the gold wire because of its strength and resistance from corrosion after a few days:
And let there be a thin thread finely woven and coarsely made according to its proportion which will fit between the teeth.
And the form of tooth setting is that you receive a thread and insert two halves thereof between healthy teeth: then move one or more threads with their extremities among the teeth, if possible without pain until completion reaches another safe side of a healed tooth through the use of the filament. Then continue to apply the texture until you reach where you first applied it; and pull with your hand using subtlety and wisdom, so that it does not remove too much: and let there be a restriction of thy thread pulling at the roots of the teeth, as being against decay.
Then incis the superfluous ends of threads with forepaws; and gather them together along one side or both sides alternately until they come to rest securely, taking care not to harm your tongue: then withdraw so strictly that it remains only while there is something left hanging between a healthy tooth.
If it breaks or comes off, then pulls them with another thread in the same way for as long a time as necessary.
And this is the form of teeth and figures regarding tooth setting for two healthy teeth which will move about like eyesight.
And when it happens that one tooth falls out or two are extracted from their places and return in different positions as we have described them; they remain hanging by the roots at rest: but this is not done unless there is a skillful maker of teeth, prudent and expert.
And when someone is suitably prepared from bones or ivory; it takes the same shape as a tooth and is set into its place whereby the decayed tooth was removed being fastened with thread: so that, remaining in this manner for some time longer while tied together by their roots they continue hanging there. But if someone does not know how to perform these things correctly or safely then he should be excluded from performing dental work on living people and animals since it is dangerous for patients as well as owners of the teeth when performed incorrectly, because untrained individuals may injure a patient by accidentally pulling out healthy teeth instead.
Chapter XXIV.
Whenever an incision occurs under the tongue it is either natural, as in where man originates from or due to some unfortunate incident that has already occurred.
And the operation is that it opens your infirmity' end mouth into its hollow and lifts up the tongue so: thereafter incises this nerve ligament through the width until the tongue detaches from holding onto itself.
If there were something hard and knotty within it; and if that had occurred because of the consolidation of an injury: then you would thrust in a hook into it through its width until reaching that ligament until hitting upon those nodes which are thus loosened by tearing.
And take care not to create a deep wound within the flesh; and thrust an arrow into it thereafter blood flows out of it..
Therefore he dips to examine the wound with rose water, vinegar or cold water.
Then he places a linen cloth under the tongue that holds an ill person throughout every night so it does not get better again..
If blood flows forth, then he places a clod of earth over the place where the wound is.. If then the blood pursues you, thereafter with a slow-burning brand of dark freckle skin used for that purpose; afterwards take care about it together with other remaining treatment until healed..

Whenever an abscess occurs beneath the tongue which is similar to a frog's skin and forbids its natural movement; sometimes it even becomes so large that one must open the mouth until exposed..

If therefore you see its flesh turn greyish-black or black and firmly established where it has no feeling to indicate sickness; then touch not the lump itself, for it is a cancer.
And if it becomes dampened and turns into a moist spot where there is no feeling; then throw away immediately the pointy end for dipping within itself with water (saturated), insert thinly woven sponges, and free it from all parts of its body. There are many kinds of goats and I have already divided all their species as follows; it is necessary that someone should understand the difference between a Goat [Nodrum] and an Exitor.
I declare that when the Exitor is heat, fever, and painful sensations which are violent until excessive boiling overflow occurs leading to decomposition; then indeed disease rests in repose.
When the Nodrum is not heat, nor fever, nor painful sensations and contains these calming medicines contained within its own sac: which in color corresponds to that of a person's body; likewise it mimics both Cicer (chickpea) and Batecha.
And they are two in kind:" either moist or dry. And the colors of this moisture vary according to what I have divided.
It is necessary then that as you approach the cure of Nodes (goats), so learn to observe it and investigate this immediately with a tool which I call Intromissus, according to what follows after here.
And the mode of inquiry is as follows for all Nodes (goats): so that you will receive this tool and place it in a moistened region which you find to be an apostate: then with your fingers, slowly digging into this gradually until you know when already penetrates through skin. But if the pus discharges during operation and it is not possible to remove the abscess cleanly then often this happens: cut off part of it externally until nothing remains except for something inside which may still be infectious (with Nodo).
Because if any foreign substance remains within it more or less the size of a pea, then frequently returns with nodule (with Nodo).
But if you are harmed by it and there remains within a little piece of foreign material: immediately cleanse this thoroughly with some saline solution (or similar), corrode superficially the wound area using one or more sharp needles which have been heated in hot oil until they become red, tie off securely at its upper end where it is hanging abnormally and place a warm poultice on this point; keep observing till it becomes healthy again (with Nodo).

But if you find that your pulse is contrary to what I have said or not pulsatile at all: promptly apply pressure, mark the area with ink where this occurs and release it slowly over two days, three days, until the abscess discharges its own matter; then return for a new examination of whatever remains from Nodo.

When the hernia occurs in the groins as we have previously stated and there is an eminent place where it does not go down into testicles: if that which has descended is little or insufficiently large, then returns at all hours; but when prolonged by time, a fissure forms on each side of the hernia until the intestine falls back in.
And it happens that when this is extended into the groins as we have previously stated. Which is because once a fissure forms in the hernia area which extends into the groins as we have previously stated; then it becomes milder and retracts back to its original place with an elevated site where there's nowhere for anything more to enter.
And the treatment of it is by a hot iron as that story has passed on.
And whenever it's treated with iron, in this way as follows; and there is, that he should lie on his back between your hands. Thereafter the treated place of hernia's retraction and elevated site is dried through a narrow incision following the size of three fingers.
Thereafter strings are tied to a part under the cloth and those which lie below being bound until an empty space is found beneath them that follows itself. Chapter fifty-eight.
About the softening of skin around testicles.
Many times the skin around the testicles is softened among certain people because they are moist with flesh that lies between them and due to their disgusting appearance.
Therefore it is necessary for him who asks for this treatment to lay the weak body on his back and make an incision over all that has been softened by nature itself.
Thereafter attach two lips with a stitch: and if urine is present, firstly drain the overflowing softened skin over three or four stitches, then firm up with an additional stitch.
Then make an incision between the stitches.
Thereafter attend to any remaining wounds: until healed as far as possible and then let go of the hairs.

Chapter on castration.
Chapter fifty-nine. In this chapter concerning castration which we have excommunicated according to our law and that I am permitted not to remember him in my book for the sake of forgetting his deed, it is sufficient only if done out of two ways: one being an act, as a wound made with iron or other hard object; another way by surgical means. This chapter concerns remedy against harm caused by castration and its aftermath.
Who is there to know when a question arises about it (medicine) and who will learn its treatment?
And another method is that we frequently subject some animals to castration for our benefit using this (surgery), as with asses, Hyrcanian stallions, and cats.
I declare that castration is performed in two ways. Or by atrophy (cessation of function)." Or through a cut or incision; and also dissection.
As for those which are subjected to attrition (cessation of function), the method is that we make an animal sit in hot water until their testicles soften and lengthen; then with your hand, they will be drawn upwards: next let them fall again by touching.
And in castrations performed through a cut or incision, you must hold the animal and press its scrotum with your left hand.
Then bind the suspensorium and after drying one side of all cuts until two come out; then when they have extruded themselves afterwards you wash them both with water: but do not leave over wetness which is on top of (the wound) to sift through like flour.
And this method of castration is better for which takes place by attrition (cessation of function): as sometimes it leaves something from the testicles, whereby desire to copulation may arise in animals.
Thereafter care one until he is cured.

About puncturing pus that occurs within the breast.

Head LXXVI.
Concerning the delivery of dead fetuses.

If you hope that the skin will still cling to it and not result from further corruption therefrom; and if flesh is thickened with decay within (caro), then care must be combined with clysters at this time as well: which concerns us concerning the Sinus.
Then if it is great and pus issuing from there gives off fetid odors; then the affected part should be washed with Egyptian clysters made of wine, oil, or honey (acetum et oleum autiniar), parts taken equally into solution: which together are boiled over fire until red meat medicines change color: and it is best to do so in swelling fullness of the milk.
Then receive from that thing which is necessary to you and dissolve it with water and honey; then clysterize the navel region of him by instilling a mixture thereof, and string his orifice while applying medicine in such quantity as for two hours' time.
Then take out the fetid stuff from it by its smell over these days until his belly is cleaned and foul odor removed.
And whenever you clysterize with ashes of the oven or ashes from pine woods (a poultice), and this medicine is not present to thee, then take that hot water down your throat: spit out all wood-ashes; pour over it a little warm broth made by boiling bark tree's leaves in water. Then drink the wine of that and clysterize with it until you believe what is to be said: That his belly has already been washed away (purified).
What if the patient cannot bear any of the Egyptian remedies or water ash but has now dissolved with honey; take that mixed in some kind of acid (excrete) and clysterize it into his navel region, which is already smeared therewith. Alternatively clysterize it with honey and wine which is melted; let the mixture stick to his belly (for cleaning), and make him sweat, so that he cleans himself: And when there are superfluous fluids or dried up skin in the drinks of wine mix, apply them on Belly especially where they dry.
Whenever you do that a few times and trust what is to be said; then clysterize with his fetid matter, which now has been cleaned away (purified), so as it may give birth of new flesh within him: And when the belly corruption (=degeneracy) lies no more in thee.
And it is so that you take what comes out of the bed-mass (leprosy), and dissolve with rose oil; melt wine over him: or clysterize his belly by means of some medicines, salves etc., which I have written about in my treatise on ointments.
If the sinax Sinus (sinus) is constricted where there is no catheter inserted: then it must be expanded as much as possible with minimal use of iron or by applying an Egyptian ointment unguento, or a basilic unguento in that place until it has been sufficiently amplified.
And similarly if the mouth is already large enough, then it must be bound together with a ligature and release whatever amount of that substance enters during its use without any additional supplement.
And similarly if there is inflammation of the sinus from which it comes out (e.g., a fistula), and blood flows upwards: then dry itself into the depressed place wherein that flow occurs, so as to stop its movement downward; for when pus becomes encapsulated within that Sinus, it does not produce new tissue in that area.
What if it is not possible for you to dry the sinus below its inferior region: then, cover that with a dressing as prepared in accordance with what enters there from the above; since when pus flows out of such Sinus, it requires material easily available and suitable according to your preparation. Cover it with something so that nothing from the pus remains within; and receive drugs solidified as described above which are directed over signs of such discharge according to its nature. Extend these upon a linen cloth. And let the width of that fabric be such as to allow complete communication with the entirety of the sinus. Then insert it into the mouth's opening directly at that sinax point with forceps, and then gradually open the sinus passage as little as possible. Then extend the linen cloth over another ointment on the sore spot to match its size and place it above in a position distant from the sinus opening; so that all flow out of exit points: you should not remove the entirety unless after drinking water for one or two days.
He who is at the mouth of the Sinus Cavity is he whose mucous membrane always discharges throughout all hours so that whatever collects therein becomes pus; and if you know whether this matter which comes from it consists chiefly, or only slightly, or not at all, of worm eggs, then [it] can be digestible, indigestible, easily treated.
And whenever considering the same place as his sinus cavity, he either does not feel pain therein or feels pain; and is paralyzed by it, or has no difficulty with it at all.
Therefore you are led to a similar kind of treatment; and when the mucous discharge comes out through his sinus cavity opening, then know that Sinus has adhered within it or approximated its wall attachment: so he should take [it] with him in the morning if necessary (or on alternate days), change clothes for a while thereafter.
